text:
These cookies are delicious and cake-like!  Every fall - it never fails - when the leaves start turning and the weather gets crisp I start getting requests for these cookies - it's crazy!  
I make a few slight changes and these cookies turn out PERFECTLY!  First of all, I add 3 drops of red food coloring to the 'wet ingredient' mixture (to liven up the pumpkin's orange color).  Second, I bake the cookies at 365 degrees for 12 minutes instead of 350 degrees for 10 minutes (which, like others have said is not NEAR enough time to allow the cookies to cook through). And thirdly I place the cookies with a medium sized scoop on a greased cookie sheet, then I slam the cookie sheet down on the table a few times to get them to spread out a little (I find the cook more evenly and also look a lot more attractive).
These cookies are served best warm straight from the oven or cold straight from the refridgerator - I wouldn't recommend letting them sit on your counter, even if they are in a covered conatainer - the time I did that they got soggy and melted a little from the heat of our wood stove.  =)

I used milk chocolate chips and took the advice of others and added 4 drops of red food dye to the wet ingredients to give it that rich pumpkin color. text:
I really love this recipe, but if you're making this for a lot of people, don't rely on the "servings calculator". for about 60 servings use this adaption, because the calculator for the ingredients makes the pumpkin dough very wet and almost soupy. here's the adaption for a bigger batch:
    * 1 large can (3 1/2  cups) of canned pumpkin
    * 3 cups of white sugar
    * 1tablespoon of vegetable oil
    * 3-eggs
    * 4-cups of self rising flour
    * 1 tablespoons of baking powder
    * 2 tablespoons of ground cinnamon
    * 1 teaspoons salt
    * 1 tablespoon of baking soda 
    * 1 tablespoon of milk
    * 1 tablespoon of vanilla extract 
    * 1 bag of semisweet chocolate chips

text:
OK I give!  I haven't been able to find a pumpkin cookie recipe that isn't cake-like so I'm just going to have to deal with it.  That said, these cookies are amazing!  I tried the "Chocolate Chip Pumpkin Cookies" recipe on this site and I thought they were good, but I think these are better.  I did, however, make a few changes to this recipe.  I used 1 tsp cinnamon, 1/2 tsp of Spice Islands' pumpkin pie spice (they're all a little different), 1/4 tsp ginger, 1/8 tsp nutmeg & 1/8 tsp cloves.  I used toasted pecans instead of walnuts and I used about 1 cup of chocolate chips.  The other recipe I used had twice as much batter and half as much chocolate chips and there was STILL too much chocolate in those cookies - you couldn't taste the pumpkin at all.  I'm telling you if you like the taste of pumpkin go VERY easy on the chocolate chips - the chocolate can really mask the pumpkin flavor.  If you love chocolate that much just make chocolate chip cookies and throw some pumpkin pie spice in the mix.  I too had to crank the oven to 375 and bake for 15 minutes, but my oven temp is kind of lame.  Other than that, this recipe is fantastic!!

text:
I modified the recipe to make it healthy yet delish. Used 2 cups whole wheat flour, 2 tsp baking powder, 1 tsp baking soda, 1 tsp cinnamon, 1/2 tsp nutmeg, 1 cup canned pumpkin, 1/2 cup brown sugar( don't pack it), 8 packets of Splenda, 1 egg, 1 tbs skim milk (not necessary to be skim but what I had on hand), 1 tbs vanilla, 1/4 cup non fat yogurt + 1/4 cup smart balance margarine for the oil, decreased the chocolate chips (dark chocolate chips) to 3/4 cup to allow the pumpkin flavor to be pronounced. I didn't add any salt to the dough because there is already salt in the margarine and I decreased the sugar so I want to avoid a salty cookie. I'm not a huge fan of nuts in my cookies so I eliminated them but you can add them if you like.If you want a more orange colored cookie, add a few drops of food coloring as well. I cooked them as directed.( 350 degrees for 10 minutes) Before putting them in the oven, I flattened them out a bit so they look prettier. Be careful not to over bake them or you'll end up with a drier cookie. Bake them just so they lose their sheen and soft in the middle. The cookies continue to cook as they cool. I loved them cold and fresh out of the oven. It tastes much more moist straight from the oven and chewier from the fridge. Definitely try them this way. It's lower in calories and yummy. Hope my review helped! =D

I made the following adjustment:

text:
I'm a newbie baker. Here are some tips I found out by my own mistakes: 1) The smallest can of pumpkin puree is 15oz, so I doubled the recipe. DO NOT make the mistake I did, and think that doubling the 2cups of Chocolate chip morsels will be okay. One cup is enough if you want to still taste the pumpkin.  2) Add nutmeg, cloves, and ginger to the spices. I added about 1 tsp each additional spice. Could not imagine what they would have been like if not added.  3) Took the advice of 365 degrees for 12 minutes, and the morsels did not even melt. If I had to do it over, i would melt the morsels first for a more even spread of chocolate. 4) make sure to chop the walnuts, but not a big deal.  I had LOTS of leftover cookie dough, so I put it in a cake pan. I think it turned out better than the cookies.

text:
These were good. I used 1/2 c white sugar and 1/2 c brown. Instead of the cinnamon, I put 1 tbsp and 1 tsp of the pumpkin spice also from this site. For half the batch I also added caramel chips. These cookies took about 30 minutes to bake instead of 10 and made about 20 medium-sized cookies for me. It was very cake-like just as other reviewers had said. A mistake on my side, but I felt like the spice over-powered the pumpkin taste. Personally, I would have preferred a little more sweetness.  Perhaps I probably would have liked milk chocolate more than semi-sweet because the spice and semi-sweetness resulted in a touch of bitterness. *UPDATE* I originally gave this a 4, but after leaving it for a few hours in the fridge, I had them again and they were delicious! :D I definitely taste that pumpkin taste I was looking for and the chocolate/spice was hardly noticable anymore. So definitely keep them chilled!!!

I would give these cookies 35 stars if I could! They are absolutely the best pumpkin cookies I've ever tasted. Those who are hesitant to try them, do not fear! The subtle spice and pumpkin flavor mixes in perfectly with the chocolate, and they have a soft, cake-like texture. I did a 1.5 batch and it made about 42 pretty big cookies. When baked on parchment paper, they were finished after about 12 minutes, minus the crunchier bottom- but I do think they rose a bit less too. They ended up perfectly orange colored, so I don't know  what happened to some other reviewers. Everyone loved them, thanks so much for the awesome cookies!!

country:

text:
First of all, AWESOME proportions (for the most part) in this recipe.  However, I made some essential changes for flavor.  I used half butter/half oil to add some richness (I know it's not as healthy) ;).  I added nutmeg, allspice, ginger, cloves, and about 1/2 cup more pumpkin for a much improved flavor.  I prefer hazelnuts to walnuts, but either is great.
Some other reviews suggest adding red food-coloring.  WHY?  I wouldn't unnecessarily give kids red food coloring (especially kids like my 7-year-old brother)!   The extra pumpkin I added improves color as well as taste.  You could also use a little red beat juice.
I also made these gluten-free by using 1 cup brown rice flour, 1 cup potato starch (could also use tapioca or corn starch), and 1 tsp guar gum in the place of the all-purpose flour.  
BEST pumpkin chocolate-chip cookies I've ever tasted!!  They really are best right out of the oven, and also very good refrigerated.  Don't store them on the counter, they're not as good.

While these pumpkin chocolate chip cookies aren't very mich like cookies in texture (or any others I've tried), they are still awesome! They are almost like pumpkin chocolate chip muffin tops - how can that be bad? My toddler also loved them. The only changes I made were due to what I had available in the house - I used cake flour (its all I had) and 1/3 cup brown sugar and 2/3 cup raw sugar (turbinado) and one tsp of cinnamon instead of two (as per reviews). I used a large cookie scoop so I had to bake them longer (about 14 min). Overall, good recipe and I will make them again and again.

text:
I made a "healthier" version of these cookies by using fewer chocolate chips and substituting apple sauce for 1/2 of the oil and whole wheat flour for 1/2 of the flour. I really liked them. They are really more cake-like than your average cookie, but there's no butter in them so it's to be expected. They don't spread at all so be sure to flatten out the dough or you'll get mini scones:). I have to agree with another reviewer in saying that they are best fresh or cold - not sitting on the counter. Enjoy!

text:
These are excellent.  2 changes to make your life easier:  Use the entire 15 oz. can of pumpkin and add an extra 1/2 cup of flour.  That way, if you're like me,  you don't have a little container of leftover pumpkin puree in your fridge that you eventually throw out.  I hate wasting food.  With this change, I get about 5 dozen cookies, making each one a generous tablespoon size.  They do not spread so feel free to load up your sheets.  I am able to get the entire load in my oven on 3 sheets at one time.  Convect bake for 20 minutes and you're DONE in under an hour!  I make these constantly in the fall for my kids' school sports teams and they are a huge hit.  Enjoy!!

Also, I got about 40 cookies from this recipe, not 2 dozen (used a teaspoon to scoop dough onto cookie sheet).  I made some changes based on what other people had written: 1) Cooked at 360 degrees Farenheit in a convection oven for 11 minutes, instead of 350 degrees for 10 minutes; 2) I added 1/4 tsp nutmeg; 3) I added lots of red and a little yellow food coloring to keep the orange color; 4) I flattened out the dough a bit when I put it on the tray so that they bake a little flatter instead of a heaping mound; 5) I smacked the tray down a few times and shook it a bit to try and get the dough to settle down before sticking in the oven; 6) I only used 15oz of pumpkin instead of 16oz because the grocery store only sold 15oz cans.

text:
These were delicious! A friend who doesn't eat many sweets managed to scarf down three of them - and then say that the only thing stopping him from eating more was that he was so full. My changes were minor: I used all whole wheat flour (the pastry kind), I used olive oil instead of vegetable, I used part white and part brown sugar, and I used a little less cinnamon and added some allspice and nutmeg to make up the difference. I used fewer chips, some dark and some milk, due to my own preference. (So maybe that sounds like a lot of changes, but they didn't seem that big at the time!) Like others, I flattened them a bit before baking, and I took them out when they looked set but not browned. They were perfect fluffy cookies bursting with bits of chocolate (but not too many!) with a lovely color. I didn't add food coloring because most are artificial, and why ruin a good cookie with something fake? Try these - they're delicious!

Good cookies, made them smaller, teaspoon size, in order to get them down to 60 calories per cookie. They didn't have as prominent a pumpkin flavor as other cookies I've made, not sure why. If I make them again I will use pumpkin pie spice instead of cinnamon. They hold their shape very well so it's easy to make lots per cookie sheet because they do not spread! I made these after visiting the Pumpkin Patch with my son, daughter-in-law and new 7 month old grandson! Fun times! UPDATE: Made them again, over 4 yrs later. I used pumpkin pie spice, 3 tsp, instead of cinnamon and that was an improvement. I also followed another bakers advice and cooked them for 12 minutes at 365, perfect! This recipe made 36 good size cookies.

text:
This is a great recipe but, like others, I made some changes:  I used 1 1/4 cup freshly roasted pumpkin; I used 4 TBSP + 1 tsp Truvia (equals 2/3 cup white sugar) and 1/3 cup brown sugar in place of the 1 cup white sugar; 2 cups whole wheat flour instead of the AP flour; 1/2 cup no sugar added apple sauce instead of the veggie oil; 1/4 tsp salt instead of 1/2 tsp salt; 1 tsp Almond Breeze instead of whole/regular milk (I no longer use cow's milk because of the sugar content); added 1 tsp pumpkin pie spice, 1/2 tsp freshly grated nutmeg and 1/2 tsp cinnamon; 1 cup chocolate chips instead of 2 cups.  All other ingredients were as posted in the original recipe.  I baked at 365 for 12 minutes and they were perfectly done!  ~~ My husband recently learned he has type 2 diabetes (diet controlled/no meds at this time) and I changed the recipe to make it have a lower glycemic value.  I will make these again in less than three weeks to take along to our family Thanksgiving dinner.  Yummy!!

These are a yummy Fall treat!  I wanted to "healthify" them, so I used 1 cup whole wheat flour, 1/2 cup all purpose, and then I grounded old-fashioned oatmeal to a powder in the Magic Blender and used that for the remaining 1/2 cup.  I used brown sugar and I cut it to 1/2 cup.  Everything else I kept the same, and I just love the texture!  They're soft, yet not doughy, and hearty but not heavy.  Mine didn't spread much at all in the oven, so I'd suggest flattening them a little bit if you don't want rounded cookies.  Oh, and I added about 1/2 tsp of fresh ground nutmeg!  I enjoyed the big dose of vanilla in these, and if you are like me and don't like overly-sweet desserts, the 1/2 cup of sugar was plenty.. and allowed for the chocolate chips to provide the subtle sweetness.  Another plus: No need for an electric mixer.. less dishes. :)  Next time, I'll sub half the oil for unsweetened applesauce (I was out of that, this time).  Thank you for an easy, quick, and delicious recipe!

text:
So I made this recipe last year and felt they came out a tad too dry.  I thought maybe I just overbaked them and just needed to take them out sooner.  I recently revisited this recipe and decided to give it another go.  After I had already mixed up the cookie dough I realized instead of just 1 cup pumpkin as the recipe says, I misread and put in 1 whole CAN (15oz, = 1 3/4 cups).  The cookies came out perfect with the extra pumpkin!  I have baked a couple batches this way and they are excellent.  Bake them for 13 minutes exactly.  Also store them in a ziplock bag and they will stay perfectly moist the way pumpkin chocolate chip cookies should be. My 5 star rating is for the recipe with the whole 15 oz can of pumpkin instead of just 1 cup.

These cookies have become a fall tradition for me. The first time I had anything like them, I was very young. My great Aunt made them for me. I started baking more as I got older and didn't have the exact recipe. After trying multiple recipes this is absolutely the winner. They taste almost exactly the same as the cookies I grew up with. I always double the recipe, too. It makes a lot of cookies but they go fast... Whatever is left after the first day, keeps very well... And the very last cookie is always just as good as the first!!!

text:
I have to say...after reading the negative reviews, I was in a complete panic as I had prepared the batter the night before and kept it in the fridge. Tempted to throw it away the next day, I took a deep breath and was glad I didn't. The cookies came out truly delicious! I agree with a few though, that if you're making THAT many changes to a recipe, it's probably not the best recipe for you. Anyway, here are some notes for some of the less drastic changes I would make next time. 1)As a chocolate lover, this recipe definitely called for too much chocolate. I would limit the morsels to 1 cup or 1 1/4cup. 2)Keep the temperature at 350 for 10 minutes! It does not need to go higher. I burned the bottoms of the first batch just by going 5 minutes over. The lumps definitely don't go down like usual cookies, so they will look deformed but they ARE cooked! 3) In a last minute panic, I threw in a few dashes of pumpkin spice (just in case) the pumpkin flavor didn't shine. I doubt a few dashes made a difference, but the pumpkin flavor was there!      No, this isn't the BEST cookie recipe out there, but to me these are pretty darn good! I'm so glad I didn't make any of the other recommended changes. This recipe seems to have its quirks already worked out :) ENJOY!!

text:
I made this with the ingredients stated, except that I added the vanilla with the egg, pumpkin, et cetera. I used a small cookie scoop which produced small little button like cookies; these cookies do not spread much, if at all.  The texture of the dough is wet and is not suitable for pressing down with glass or fingers. I tried to refrigerate dough, hoping to firm it up, but to no avail.  When I made the recipe I thought the ratio of chocolate chips seemed high and I was correct.  After baking and sampling I thought there were way too many chocolate chips; next time I will halve the amount.  The chips seemed to distract away from the pumpkin flavor.  I do like the suggestion I read in one of the other reviews of slamming the baking sheet down on the counter a few times to spread them out a bit.  Next time I will use a larger scoop.  These definitely are more cake like in texture; I would store them with the lid off, or refrigerate, or they will turn to mush. This was my first attempt at a pumpkin chocolate chip cookie and it won't be my last.  These were good, maybe great, but not exactly what I was looking for.  I may even suggest adding some rolled oats to give a more substantial texture.

text:
Let's get a couple of things out of the way: 1) these are very much cake-like cookies.  Know this going in, so you don't get to come back later reviewing that these are too cake-y :).  Enjoy them for what they are.  My daughter called them muffies because they were like muffin-cookie hybrid.  2) This is really a chocolate chip recipe.  Let's face it, if you put a full bag of chocolate chips in a batch of rolled up play-doh, chocolate lovers will rejoice.  The pumpkin is NOT the feature here.  I put 5 drops of red food color in just so people would know that they weren't only chocolate chip.  We like them, but I wish pumpkin were more primary than a chocolate chip.  Edit add: Do what you can to help flatten a bit before cooking like bang the sheet on the counter to help them cook through.  Needed 12 minutes in my oven.  This is the first cookie I have ever preferred cold out of the fridge.

text:
These are AMAZING. I gave some out to at least 10 different people, and the looks on their faces after taking their first bite were priceless. Half of those people immediately asked me to send them the recipe. This is definitely the recipe to follow for pumpkin chocolate chip cookies. I've made them twice already, but have not tried them with the walnuts yet; however, I'm sure they are good that way as well! Pumpkin is always a great ingredient for cookies because it keeps them softer for longer, and if you like them extra soft the trick is to set the temp. 25 degrees lower. Also, these are really good on both extremes: cold or warmed up in the microwave.

text:
This recipe is really good.  I made it last night and doubled the recipe.  I used half wheat flour and half all-purpose.  I also used half vegetable oil and half applesauce.  I used 3 1/2 t cinnamon and 1 t each of cloves, ginger and nutmeg (keep in mind that I doubled the recipe).  I also added some red food coloring as others suggested.  I cooked them at 365 for 12 1/2 minutes.  Next time I make this, I will use about the same amount of cinnamon, but will cut in half the amount of the other 3 spices.  The cookies are awesome, but the spices are a bit overwhelming.  I also think I will reduce the amount of chocolate chips I use by maybe one fourth.  Call me weird, but I think they are a bit too chocolatey.  I love the taste and texture of the pumpkin and think it would be a bit more enjoyable with a little less of the chocolate chips. Overall, though, fantastic recipe!

text:
Short review: Great cookies, but READ THE REVIEWS HERE FIRST!!!!  You'll pick up many tips which will make the cookies FABULOUS!    Long Review:   These cookies were AMAZING!  I, too, altered the recipe after reading all the other reviews.  I used 1/2 cup of white sugar and 1/2 cup of brown (though next time I will use just brown sugar) in place of just white sugar, 1/2 cup of butter in place of the oil, just under 1 teaspoon of cinnamon, 1/4 teaspoon each of clove, nutmeg and ginger, 1/4 teaspoon of salt and about 1/2 a cup of chocolate chips.  We also added 4 drops of red food colouring.    I'm glad I made half of the batch without chocolate chips!  The ones without the chips were INSANELY AMAZING!  They didn't last more than 15 minutes.  We used mini chocolate chips and very few of them, but the chocolate still seemed to overpower all of the other flavours.  We actually still have a couple of the chocolate chip ones left.    I added the vanilla and food colouring to the wet mixture when I put the egg in, rather than put them in at the end.  I also baked them at 365 for 10-12 minutes and flattened them 2 minutes before taking them out, which made them more cookie-like.    Overall, very good cookies after you alter the recipe!  I will DEFINITELY be making these again for our big Halloween party, but without the chocolate chips.

text:
These are 'okay' cookies.  They get 3 stars because after the first batch I had to add spices in myself, they were VERY bland before this and bordered on 1 star.  I was lucky to have pumpkin pie spice on hand so I didn't have to individually add in all the recommended ones.  This also says it yields 2 dozen but I'm wondering what size cookies the original poster was making, were they for bigfoot?  If you go by standard sizes and not super sizes our country is based on, this single recipe can yield up to 4 dozen cookies but if you are looking to follow exactly, your cookies will be huge.  Again saying it's an 'okay' recipe because it would make a better 'blondie brownie' type recipe than a 'cakie cookie'.  Cakie cookies aren't popular amongst children and the masses but put in the right setting (ie brownie-type) I can see them quickly gobbled up (again if you add spices so they can have flavor).  Another thing, ALWAYS add flour last regardless of what the recipe calls for, this is baker's knowledge.  Adding fluids to the flour batter prior to combining all ingredients together only gives you a rough batter and harder cookies (or cake, etc).

city:

region:

country:
None
text:
Yep, theses cookies are by far the best of any pumpkin chip I've ever had. Truthfully, I think they're now my favorite cookie. I did make a few small tweaks. First, add a tsp or more of pumpkin spice, it really helps change it from good to amazing. Second, I've found this cookie is so great why just enjoy it one way? So, I separate my batter into three bowls. Into the largest portion I add a lot of white chocolate chips - once baked these are best eaten cold straight out of the refrigerator. The second portion of batter gets milk chocolate chips - this is my husbands favorite and it also great straight out of the fridge or nuked in the microwave for like 20 seconds. The third batter gets semi-sweet chocolate and these are by far best when heated in the microwave (again for like 20 seconds) so that the chocolate is gooey. I do store all of them in a covered container in the refrigerator. Be generous when adding your chocolate chips, more definitely is better and I'm a person who usually uses less than recommended for traditional chocolate chip cookies, but the cookie consistency and pumpkin flavor really are best when paired with the chocolate. Enjoy!!

text:
Fantastic! I altered the recipe to my taste and made cookie bars. I took these to my community group and they were gobbled up so quickly! Even my picky husband liked them. And here's the strange thing -- I liked them because I love pumpkin. DH liked them because he felt like they weren't too "pumpkin-y." Go figure. My Changes: Used a whole can of pumpkin (seemed silly to waste half the can, plus I like the taste of pumpkin); I used brown sugar instead of white sugar and this yielded a good flavor and color; doubled the cinnamon; also, I just added the baking soda to the dry ingredients, I didn't see any need to dissolve it in milk. Worked fine for me. I spread it in a greased 9x11 glass pan and baked at 350 degrees for twelve minutes. My oven runs hot, so ten minutes may be enough for most. They turned out great!

text:
These were SO deliciously addictive!  My only warning would be that by no stretch of the imagination could this recipe only make '12 servings'...I read that, and since I was making these for my 1st grader's Halloween party, I decided to double it (from other reviews I read, I didn't double the cinnamon, only put in slightly more than the single recipe called for, and I also followed another reviewer's advice and used chocolate mini-chips, both of which worked great).  Anyway, I ended up with probably 80 cookies of various sizes...some about tablespoon sized (for the kids party), some about twice that size, and some that were about as large as my palm...they all came out to the same cake-like consistency, which I loved!  My kids thought they were like a cross between a cookie and a muffin.  Oh, also, I did as another reviewer suggested and added a couple drops of red food coloring to make the cookie dough a little more orange.  Fantastic recipe, I'm sure these will be asked for a few more times before the end of the year!

text:
These are awesome! Like another reviewer I created more of a pumpkin pie spice mixture as opposed to just using cinnamon and baked at about 365 for 12 minutes.  As soon as the batter is mixed they're fine to bake but they came out much better after letting the batter sit in the fridge for a day. This made it easier to drop/mold into cookie shapes and to flatten them slightly. If they're cooked according to the recipe they would probably make decent muffins. The spices (nutmeg, cinnamon, clove, allspice) really brought out the pumpkin flavor and went well with the chocolate chips and walnuts.

Very yummy.  Would make great holiday gifts for family and friends.

This is a great "fall" cookie.  I did make a few modifications.  Instead of canned pumpkin I used fresh and substitued olive oil for the veg oil. I also added nutmeg, ginger, cloves, and used less cinn.  I used special dark chocolate chips and used pecans instead of walnuts.  Before baking I used a glass dipped in sugar, a touch of cinnamon and nutmeg and GENTLY pressed the cookie (something my grandma used to do).  They look beautiful and tasted even better!  I turned the temp up on the oven as well.

text:
Through the years, these cookies have been an autumn favorite in my family.  This recipe is perfect. The texture of the cookie is soft, but not so soft as to be muffin-like.  They are still firm enough to be a good, packable cookie. Although I wouldn't change the recipe itself, I would change the baking temp to 365, as in a previous review.  10 minutes was perfect for me, with two cookie trays in a convection oven.  One bonus with this style of cookie- the cookies DO NOT spread that much at all, so you can bake more on one tray.  And with two large trays in the oven, I made the whole batch at once.

text:
I just made this recipe tonight, and I couldn't stop eating the cookies. The cookies were moist and flavorful.
I did make some alterations to the recipe though.  
I used 1/2 cup of clover honey instead of 1 cup white sugar.
I used 1/2 cup unsweetened apple sauce instead of 1/2 cup oil.
I used 1 cup all purpose flour AND 1 cup whole wheat flour.
Also, I halved the batter. In one half, I only used the cinnamon to spice the batter.  In the other half, I used nutmeg, cloves, allspice, and ginger in addition to the cinnamon. 
I personally liked the addition of these other spices best.  Especially the cloves.
I think next time I will try to include cardamom or nuts.
Also, I would like to try molasses as a sweetner next time...or orange blossom honey (which actually tastes like oranges). 
This recipe is easy to make and delicious.

text:
I substituted half the oil with unsweetened applesauce (isn't that one of the best tricks ever?), decreased the cinnamon to 1 1/2 tsp, added 1/2 tsp nutmeg, and definitely added chopped walnuts. I decreased the amount of chocolate chips to 1 cup, and glad I did -- the chocolate has a tendency to overpower the pumpkin and spices. As the original recipe notes, they are better cold -- helps the spice flavors come through. Next time, and there will be a next time, as these are yummy, I will use white chocolate instead of semi-sweet dark. I served these to my students (they are adults), and there were polite raves all around, but my husband and I loved them. A sophisticated cookie! Thanks so much! Update: made again and substituted white chocolate for semi-sweet, and over-baked them a bit -- we loved this version, as the white chocolate didn't compete with the spices as the chocolate had.

My roommate and I went to a pot luck several weeks ago and brought these cookies with us.  *Luckily* we saved a few and left them at home because they were eaten in record time by our friends.  We made some slight modifications per other reviewers' suggestions.  We used 1 tsp of pumpkin pie spice and 1 tsp of cinnamon instead of two of the latter and we also used milk chocolate chips.  At first we were concerned that they were undercooked but the firm up when the cool.  They are fabulous cold with a glass of milk. Several people at the pot luck tried to recreate them (with other recipes) on their own but said ours were better. This recipe makes delicious cookies!

Yummy! They turned out as a soft round, fat, cake-like cookie.  I liked that they called for a liquid fat rather than a solid one-- more heart healthy.  The pumpkin also tosses in a good dose of Vitamin A-- a cookie with less guilt!    I did alter the recipe by using 1/2 white and 1/2 brown sugar, added a little ginger and nutmeg, and used pecans instead of walnuts.  I used a small scoop (1 1/2 tb) and this recipe made about 5 dozen cookies. I think, with their more delicate texture, they would have been good with mini chips.  My kids loved them.   I had a hard time keeping their grubby little fingers out of them so I could take them to an event we were attending.

I made two batches of these cookies. The first batch I made exactly as written, and they were good but not great- 4/5 stars. These cookies are REALLY tasty!  I was watching my friend's 2 sons while she was having surgery and asked them if they would like to bake some cookies.  The oldest told me yes, and asked for Pumpkin Chocolate Chip cookies "like my Mom makes."  My heart melted, and I said "Of course we can."

This was the first recipe I saw.  It looked simple enough, so I thought I'd give it a try.  The 4-year-old and 8-year-old were able to help, and we had the dough ready to put in the oven in about 10 minutes.  I baked mine for 9 minutes, and they were perfect.  We ate ours hot out of the oven; the chips were melty goodness, and the pumpkin cookie was soft, cakey, and scrumptious.  After 3 batches came out of the oven my children husband, myself and our 3 visitors had eaten all but 8 cookies.  This recipe is a keeper!

text:
Very good, cakey cookies.  I normally make a recipe exactly as written, but I read the reviews and seemed to agree ahead of time, that this batter would need more cinnamon, some nutmeg, and cloves, possibly some ginger (which I did not add, but will the next time).  I doubled the recipe because this recipe says it makes enough for 12 servings.  I didn't know if that meant only 12 cookies?  Those would've been gone in no time, so I doubled it and ended up with a boat-load of cookies....approximately 48!  So, I believe the serving size is incorrect.  I used white choc chips because I didn't have choc chips on hand and they are delish!  So, with adding more cinnamon, a teaspoon of nutmeg and cloves (to my doubled recipe), this recipe was VERY good and my kids love them.  I would probably subtract some sugar, though.  A little too sweet if that's such a thing :).

text:
This is a great cookie! Easy to make and perfect for fall. 

Made just as listed and the cookie is very cake like. Almost spongy. After some other pumpkin cookie experiments I have found that this is a feature of using pumpkin - it makes cookies more dense and cakey. A simple substitution made the cookies a bit more cookie like. I subbed out vegetable oil and used butter instead - the exact same amount. And for a little more flavor I doubled the cinnamon and then added half as much ground ginger (so 4 tsp cinnamon and 2 tsp ground ginger). The result is a yummy, moist, flavorful cookie with the perfect amount of fall flavor. With these adjustments this cookie is, for me, perfect and a permanent fixture in my recipe book!

text:
As written, I give these a 4. To elevate them to a 5+, here's what I did: 

*Used butter instead of oil (personal preference)
*used half brown, half white sugar
*used half cinnamon, half pumpkin pie spice 
*decreased chocolate chips to 1 to 1.5 cups (I know, I can't believe I'm saying that, either)

I creamed the softened butter, then added the wet ingredients and mixed well (in my kitchenaid). Combined the dry ingredients in a separate bowl and added them to the wet. Mixed well, then stirred in chocolate chips. 12 min at 350.

These were really moist and delicious- and a little different from the typical chocolate chip cookie! It's true what others have said- they are more of a "cakey" cookie. I followed the advice of some others and added red food coloring. I doubled the recipe and added 7 drops - could have used more to make them just a bit more orange. I would definitely make these cookies again in the fall.

text:
As written this is very good. I made a second based on reviewer suggestions, my hubby and I replaced the oil with Apple sauce, we used only 1 teaspoon of cin,we added 1 teaspoon pumpkin pie spice, and 1 teaspoon of nutmeg and reduced the chocolate chip to 1 cup these where amazing! The recipe as written at least for us had to many chocolate chips, it did overpower the pumpkin flavoring of the cookie. If your hesitating about substituting the oil for Apple sauce don't, both tasted great, you do not taste apple flavoring if your curious. We actually preferred it with apple sauce, seemed to bring out the pumpkin flavoring, and seemed lighter! Highly recommend!

I searched for a pumpkin cookie recipe and decided to try this one. I read some reviews and decided to add pumpkin pie spice, more cinnamon, and a little more nutmeg.Plus I added about 1-2 more tablespoons of flour because it seemed so wet after mixing. I was out of choc. chips so instead I made a chocolate ganache with some melting chocolate I had. I poured it over the cookies and let it run down sides--delicious. I liked the cake like texture and next  time I am planning to use this recipe to make pumpkin whoopie pies--the texture will be perfect and I will pour them out a little thinner, make the cream filling and sandwich between cookies...mmmmm, I can taste them now. text:
My kids love this recipe. Of course, I don't tell them it has pumpkin in it. Been using fresh pumpkin for over a year and this recipe is always a hit! We have used multiple types of chocolate chips over the past year and find that white chocolate are our favorite. It has a higher melting point than milk chocolate, so the kids don't get all covered with chocolate while eating their new favorite cookies (which is a good thing when you have kids with special needs and "messy" means meltdowns). They are cake-like in texture and are great fresh from the oven or cold from the fridge. Great recipe! I've shared it with numerous friends and it's now a go-to recipe for cookies all year long (as long as I've got frozen pumpkin, we've got pumpkin cookies).

text:
Well, I did make some changes, but what I really HAD to change was the bake time. My cookies came out just right at 17 minutes, which is much longer than the prescribed. At 10, they were still mush. I also did not find it necessary to grease the baking sheet.

My changes: substituted coconut oil for half the oil; substituted spelt flour for half the all purpose; I only used 1/2 the cinnamon for a more subtle flavor.

My suggestions: butterscotch chips with pecans; white chocolate chips with almonds.

text:
My family loves these cookies!  
I have altered the original recipe some: I substitute no sugar added applesauce for the vegetable oil and use 1 cup of whole wheat flour and 1 cup of white flour (using all whole wheat makes them pretty "grainy") instead of 2 cups white flour.  
Also, I use a whole bag of the mini-semisweet chocolate chips.  
I have found (by not following the directions as closely as I should have!) that if you go ahead and add the milk and vanilla to the pumpkin mixture and the baking soda to the flour mixture, that the cookies turn out the same as when you separate them out like the original recipe says to do.  
They are very cake-like cookies, nice, thick and hearty and I end up having to bake my at a higher temp. and longer than the original recipe: 375 for 12 minutes, although it may just be my oven...

text:
These turned out as expected and delicious. The pumkpin flavor is subtle. As other reviews mentioned, they are cake-like cookies. They're more fluffy than chewy - almost a muffin top consistency. I used 1/2 cup of butter instead of oil, and I added 1/4 tsp ground cloves and 1/4 tsp nutmeg. I also added 1/2 tsp cream of tartar for the cracked effect, but it didn't make a noticeable difference this time. I used butterscotch chips instead of chocolate. And finally, I ended up leaving these in the oven a bit longer than suggested, but maybe that's just my oven (around 14-15 minutes based on when the edges were just golden brown and the top of cookies were spongy/firm).

I saw this recipe and thought "There are a few reviews saying these are 'too cake-like', so why not turn them into muffins?"

Instead of a spoonful on a cookie sheet, I roughly doubled the amount, halfway filling greased muffin tins or ungreased cupcake papers, and baked for around 14 minutes. 

Incredibly moist and fluffy, whether you keep them as cookies or convert them into cupcakes, and definitely a keeper!

text:
I made these yesterday for dessert with my family.They were a BIG hit... There's none  leftover! I modified it a bit for my dad who is diabetic- used Splenda for baking, semisweet chocolate chips, and 1/2 cup applesauce to omit the need for oil. I also wanted it to be spiced more similarly to pumpkin pie, so I added a shake of ginger and a shake or two of allspice in addition to two heaping teaspoons of cinnamon. There's no need to add food coloring as others suggest, just use high quality canned pumpkin.  They're so moist and flavorful! My neighbors were raving about them, my dad took the rest home, and my husband must have eaten 8 of them. To make them neater, I used a cookie scoop and placed them as rounded scoops on parchment paper. They're best, in my opinion, just out of the oven!!

text:
These are very good, but I will admit, I've never had pumpkin cookies before.  They are cake-like and I can't even imagine a way to put pumpkin into cookies that would end up crispy.
I did add a few drops of red coloring and I think the color came out well.  They don't look abnormally orange, just more like you would expect.  I baked at 365 for 12 min which seemed perfect. I also cut down on the chocolate chips and added nutmeg and cloves and cut back on the cinnamon.  I ended up with too much cloves flavor even though I used a small pinch.  I also agree with the comment about either eating them warm or sticking them in the fridge to keep them from getting sticky.
I will probably make these again next year, but I also didn't think they were amazing.

These were definitely tasty. However, I made the mistake of making of balls of dough on the cookie sheet too large and they came out like soft scones, nonetheless, the flavor was amazing! I added pumpkin spice, some nutmeg and some cloves in addition to the cinnamon.  I also added a few tablespoons of maple syrup.  I also used 1/2 C white & 1/2 C brown sugar and 1 C white & 1 C wheat flour.    I don't think I used quite 2 C of chocolate chips, I just eye-balled it, then added 3 or 4 extra chocolate chips to each cookie as it was about to go into the oven.  I omitted the nuts. 

Everyone gave me rave reviews, aside from my husband who does not like cake, which these cookies resemble.

text:
These are pretty good. I halved the recipe due to the amount of the ingredients I had on hand, except then I added a whole egg instead of half for obvious reasons and added a bit more flour to balance the wet and dry ingredients. I realized halfway through mixing everything that the recipe called for baking soda, not just baking powder. So after searching a bit on the internet, I added approximately 3 times the baking powder as the recommended baking soda amount in addition to the baking powder already in the recipe. Despite the changes in chemistry, the cookies are actually really good. There's a bit much of the baking powder taste, but that's obviously my fault. I can tell if I had baked according to the actual recipe, the cookies would be even better. Great taste and texture. [update] I made another halved recipe with all of the correct ingredients and loved them!

These just came out of my oven and I'm not too impressed. They are overly cake-like, and are not especially pretty to look at. Most importantly, the chocolate chips just don't work (and I LOVE chocolate) with the pumpkin flavor. text:
I changed flour to 1 1/3 all purpose plus 2/3 cup bean flour.  1tsp cinnamon 1 1/2 pumpkin pie spice and baked at 360 for 14 minutes.  I immediately moved them to cooling racks and let the cookie sheet cool before next batch.  I live at about 5400 feet and they came out just perfect.  They have a light cake texture and hold together well.  Next time I may try reducing the oil a little and see what happens.  The bean flour adds fiber and protein and does not change the flavor.

text:
These were pretty good!  I used fresh pumpkin puree, so the color was lighter than if I had used the canned solid pack.  Also, I found I only had milk chocolate chips on hand so I used those and omitted the nuts from the first sheet.  The cookies were very cake-like, but I really thought they lacked flavor at first - I figured maybe it was the combination of my using fresh pumpkin and milk chocolate, which I'm really not a fan of.  So, I added chopped walnuts and the second sheet came out better, but still not great.  I added some cinnamon chips to the rest and THOSE - with the milk chocolate chips, walnuts and cinnamon chips - were by far the best.  I think for my tastes I'll definitely use semi-sweet chocolate chips next time, but I think I'll also still add in cinnamon chips for some oomph!  Ended up enjoying this cookie very much - Thanks for sharing!

text:
Everyone who has eaten these cookies has loved them, and then asked for the recipe!
A few tips:
1. don't use applesauce instead of oil, the cookies come out more like bread and are too tough.
2. substitute mini reeses pieces, or peanut butter chips for the chocolate chips. Sounds weird, but tastes delicious.
3. as you take cookies out of the oven, or a minute before, flatten cookies with a spatula. This way they look more like cookies than little puffs. Also, I think they taste better.
All around a great recipe and I love that it doesn't have butter in it!

This is the first recipe I made using homemade pumpkin puree and they are great!  My only change was to leave out the walnuts.  One bit of advice:  If you let the dough get cold, adjust the cooking time.  The ones that were room temperature cooked perfectly at 10 minutes.  The ones I had put in the fridge were doughy and dense when cooked for 10 minutes.

I made just a couple of changes to this great cookie recipe. I added 1 tsp. cinnamon and 1/2 tsp. pumpkin pie spice. I also added a few drops of red food coloring too. The batter was very thin and I added about 3/4 cup flour. The recipe easily makes two dozen cookies by using a small cookie dough scoop. The time specified was exactly right in my oven. 350 degrees for 10 minutes.

text:
I like this recipe. It was the first time I had ever made pumpkin anything. It turned out great. 
I took the advice of another review and cut the amount of spices to 1 3/4 teaspoon. For the spices, I used about 3/4 teaspoon cinnamon and 1 teaspoon pumpkin pie spice. 
The mix itself was extremely easy to drop onto the cookie sheets. As another review warns, the shape the dough is in when it enters the oven is the shape it comes out in. I just used to small spoons to round off the cookies and they came out fine. 
I will definitely be baking these again near the holidays. Thank you!
